text:
We thought this was quite good -- a nice change from so many of the crockpot recipes that use canned cream soup as a base. The combination of spices and herbs sounds strange, but combined to make a nice, rich, herby flavor. Used the listed amounts of all the spices, w/a few exceptions: I replaced the tbsp of garlic powder w/onion powder (since I used 2 lrg cloves of fresh garlic crushed in my garlic press). I also seemed to be out of basil & oregano, so used nearly a tbsp of Italian seasoning. Also used more than 1 cup of broth, but less than the whole can, since I was cooking 6 chops inst. of 4. I cooked on low for 8 hours -- smelled SO delicious when I got home from work, and my husband wondered what smelled so great when he got home. The sauce was great over steamed rice and the meat was tender and flavorful. Even the kids liked it. All in all, a very easy, tasty recipe -- I will make this again. Would also be good w/a small pork roast.

text:
What a wonderful crock pot recipe! I used six pork chops (medium thickness) a complete can of chicken stock, and all of the spices called for. (okay... maybe a bit more!) I did use onion powder instead of garlic powder. Cooked on high for 5 hours. I removed the pork chops and covered to keep warm, while I made a gravy with the liquid. I strained the liquid through a mesh strainer to remove the garlic and large spices, mixed together with a corn starch and water mixture. It made a WONDERFUL gravy that I served over the pork chops along with steamed rice and peas.  EASY recipe that I will absolutely make again and again!!

text:
Good, for a crock pot recipe.  I find it hard to get the perfect, "fall-off-the-bone yet not too dry" texture that I like - I think crock-pots vary so it's diffictult to gage.  I do not reccomend "basting" as the recipe calls for, as that defeats the purpose of using a crock pot - you do not want heat to escape until the very end.  This was good and easy, but not the best way to cook a flavorful pork chop.  Do it, if you need something easy.

text:
By far the best porkchop I have EVER EVER tasted!  I am not a huge pork fan and have steered away from porkchops most of my life...but these were AMAZING!  They smelled absolutely heavenly while cooking and we all couldn't wait to eat at dinner time!  When it was time to serve them, they fell right off the bone!  Could barely scoop them out of the crock pot without them falling apart!  My father-in-law and fiance raved over these porkchops forever...saying that they were the best they have ever tasted as well!  I cut slices into the raw chop and sprinkled with garlic powder, salt, and pepper and pan fried for a few minutes on each side in a tablespoon of vegetable oil to just brown and get some flavor in the chop.  I also did add a little Italian Seasoning instead of just Oregano, as well as a bit of onion powder to the liquid mixture.  We saved the juice that the chops cooked in and froze it because it was so good we couldn't just trash it...will probably try and experiment with it cooking something else...or just maybe add it to the mix next time we cook chops.  Will definitely be making these again...in the very NEAR future!

text:
These were truly phenomenal.  I didn't have garlic, so replaced both the garlic powder and the garlic with garlic salt.  Replaced the poultry seasoning with some crushed rosemary, a dash of nutmeg and some freshly ground black pepper.  I also added some whole shiitake mushrooms which came out almost tastier than the meat!  Once the pork chops were cooked, I removed them from the slowcooker, added a bit of cornstarch mixed with cold water and cooked on high for a minute or two until thickened.  Sauce was delicious over whole grain rice!

text:
I made half this recipe for Hubs and me last night.  I used bone-in pork chops and first browned them in a little oil.  I didn't use any additional oil.  I removed the chops to the slow cooker and deglazed my pan with the chicken broth/seasoning liquid and poured it over the chops.  I saw no need to cut slits in the chops, so I skipped that step.  I cooked these on low for 6 hours.  I strained the cooking liquid and thickened it with a cornstarch/water slurry.  I then added a tablespoon of butter and I had a delicious gravy to serve over the chops.  This was very good and one I would definitely make again, in part because Hubs couldnâ€™t stop raving about it.

Tried this recipe today after reading through many of the reviews.  It was really good.  I agree that need to use very little oil.  I used 1/2 chopped onions instead of garlic powder - used fresh garlic.  I used two cans of chicken stock because many stated it dried out and mine had to cook for 8 hours.  I sauted my garlic and onions last night and mixed everything together in the crock pot and put in frig overnight.  Cooked on low for 8 hours and was perfect.  Used the liquid to make brown rice and that was absolutely worth making the recipe for what it did for that rice.  Easy recipe and very flavorful. This goes in the lineup! - Sandra

text:
Happened upon this recipe quite by accident when I discovered that the pork roast I had defrosted was actually 2 pork chops... Since I only had 2 I cut the seasonings in half but used the same amount of broth and oil. I have been searching for YEARS for a recipe that would give me tender, juicy, pork chops and not just a chewy, dry mess. I have not been successful until now. These pork chops FELL apart, cut with a fork, and were SOOOO juicy and flavorful. It was like heaven in my mouth. The reason I gave it 4 stars is because of the oil. Combined with the fat from the chop that cooked down it was just too rich in the oil department. I will definitely make this again, will probably be my go to pork chop recipe, but I will either decrease the oil or leave it out all together and will half the spices again because it was just enough flavor to not drown out the pork like some other reviewers stated.

I am quite impressed with this recipe, although I did change a few things the second time I cooked it.  I cut back slightly on the paprika to 3/4 tbsp as I felt 1 tbsp was somewhat overpowering.  I've never added the poultry seasoning - just a sprinkle of montreal steak spice in lieu.  I felt it needed more broth, but rather than add two packets with two cups of water, I simply added one packet to 1 Â¼ cups of water to avoid the extra salt.  And I added more minced garlic rather than garlic powder.  Fresh sliced mushrooms and finely chopped onions topped off this recipe.  Once cooked, I thickened it slightly with cornstarch â€“ goes great with mashed or riced potatoes.

text:
The reason this is five star is because the amount of work is so small for such a great payoff.  The taste is excellent (don't add the oil or reduce significantly because you don't need it and it doesn't really need any extra salt).  The meat turns out very tender and it is so easy.  My kids and husband, I am feeding 5 boys, like it best when I make a gravy out of the sauce (just make extra sauce, a quick roux and add some milk) and serve it up with mashed potatoes, corn, carrots, etc.  Also great with rice and vegetables.  As other reviews mention you can change it up a lot with good results.

text:
This recipe is DELICIOUS! This was one of the first "real meals" I made for my husband and it is already a staple favorite. I usually double the recipe to cover the "family pack" pork chops I buy, because leftovers are our best friend. I don't have garlic powder or poultry seasoning so I just throw in an extra garlic clove and use 2 tsp each oregano, basil, and season salt, almost 2 tbsp paprika, 1/2 cup olive oil, as well as about 1 1/2 cups broth. I also add splashes of balsamic vinegar to taste (or smell, rather), as another reviewer suggested, and my personal theory is that it's the balsamic that really makes the dish. It's fantastic!

text:
Surprisingly good for something so simple!  My fiance was doubtful about the whole idea of slow cooker pork chops, but he was converted.  I added extra chicken broth, half a chopped onion, two teaspoons onion powder, juice from half a lemon, and one teaspoon of paprika instead of three.  I also browned the pork chops in some butter before adding them to the slow cooker, and then deglazed the pan afterwards using more chicken broth and adding that as well.  
Cooked it on low for six hours and it was terrific!!  Very tangy, savory, yummy, and delicious.  So tender and flavorful.  Be sure to adjust the salt and pepper before serving -- using bone-in pork chops also helps.  Will definitely make again.  Fiance ended up licking his plate!

text:
Delicious! I think there was too much oil, and I think the spices may have been too much (there was a slightly bitter aftertaste). Still, they tasted wonderful, and I will be making these regularly. Next time, I will use a little less oil, increase the broth to compensate, and maybe add some brown sugar to offset the bitterness. Perfect with a starchy side! I also would skip the basting process. I was out of the house the whole time, so I couldn't baste it, but I think that might be why they didn't dry out like some people are complaining about. Leave the lid on - don't let the moisture escape!
As the recipe is posted, I give it 4 stars. Some very minor adjustments make this a 5-star recipe that I would serve to company.

This was great. I coupled it up with a Portobello mushroom gravy to top it with. Chops were so tender they were like butter. Just a little hint, try grilling the chops with mesquite first with a 1 1/2 to 2 inch chop T bone type, I used this dry rub for 8 hours before putting them on the grill,
    3 tablespoons sweet paprika, preferably Spanish
    1 tablespoon freshly ground black pepper
    1 tablespoon coarse salt, either kosher or sea salt
    3/4 teaspoon sugar
    3/4 teaspoon chili powder
    3/4 teaspoon granulated garlic or garlic powder
    3/4 teaspoon onion powder
    1/4 to 1/2 teaspoon ground cayenne

text:
VERY tasty! First, I adjusted the amount of liquid because I was making twice the amount of pork chops. They were all boneless and at least an inch thick. Second, I tweaked it a bit just because I had some veggies that needed to be used before they went bad, so I added some baby carrots and an onion and layered the chops on top. Third, there were some mentions of the "gravy" being too thin, so before I added the meat, I dredged them in some seasoned flour (just salt & pepper)to thicken up the liquid as it cooked. The only reason I didn't give it five stars was because I thought there was too much oil. It made the gravy part a little greasy - but that's easily fixed. Next time, I'll just not double the amount of oil. Additionally, this is SO easy to prepare! If you don't have poultry seasoning, just add some rosemary, thyme and onion powder. I cooked it on high for about five hours and they came out deliciously tender. Will definitely make again - with less olive oil! :-)

I followed the recipe almost 100%....only one thing I changed was opt out of garlic powder and add one more garlic clove since I prefer to use fresh ingredients.  So, I think it is still fair to give this recipe rating.  We are only 2 people in our house, and I used 2 thin pork chops and added lots of veggies.  So, I kept exact amount the recipe calls for (4 servings).  I added 2 carrots (peeled but not cut), 2 stalks of celery (cut in half), 1 large onion (sliced really thick to keep its shape), 1 potato (roughly chopped).  I thickened soup and poured on pork shops.  To give a plate more color, I cooked fresh green beans and broccoli as well. Served with brown rice.  My hubby loved it and told me to keep the recipe! Thanks for the recipe!

Fantastic! I was looking for something a little different than my husband's barbecued pork sirloin steaks (though those are always great as well), and ran across this recipe.  I alternated sauce and steaks to ensure some of the spices would be trapped in between.  When they came out they were falling apart and full of flavor.  

I took all of the meat out of the crockpot after cooking and emptied the remaining contents (unstrained) into a sauce pot and added water and flour to make a gravy which was served over garlic mashed potatoes.

A HIT!  My husband, father and daughter cleaned their plates and came back for more.  All that was left was a few cups of gravy which I froze on request for some future dinner.

Fabulous! This was soooo easy and sooo good.  The only changes I made were that I didn't have poultry seasoning so I used thyme and sage and instead of canned chicken broth, I used the broth I in the freezer last time I boiled a chicken for a recipe.  I think it was 2 cups, but that worked well because the juice covered the chops. I don't have much time in the morning, so I prepared the chops in the crockpot and put them in the fridge the night before.  In a seperate bowl I put all the flavorings.  In the morning I just poured the flavorings over the chops and turned it on (med for 8 hrs). Definitely will use this recipe many more times.  I think next time I will trim most of the fat off the chops so there will be less grease.  I like adding the olive oil though because of flavor and the health benefits.

These were so tasty!  I may not ever make pork chops any other way.  And my house smelled fantastic...enough that while I was sitting on the front porch with my neighbors, they commented on the wonderful smells emanating from the house.  Made the pork chops on Monday night, it's Thursday and I am using this recipe to do chicken breasts.  The only changes I made were : I had no garlic (how does that happen!?) so subbed garlic powder. Sure smells great!

text:
Good recipe but of course like any good cook I made my adjustments. I marinade the chops overnight with a pork rub (instead of the poultry seasoning) and the olive oil and garlic. Then in the morning I browned them and throw it in the slow cooker and sautee onions in the same pan and throw in the slow cooker. I had the basil and oregano but I had a nice herb mix seasoning so I used that instead (really you can play with all the herbs you want and never go wrong)Then I added the chicken broth (no exact measure, just enough to cover the chops in the crock pot) and added the paprika and very important I added half can of tomato sauce. Paprika alone don't do it for me for the color and consistency of the sauce so to me is very important to add the tomato sauce. The pork chops turned out yummy!!

text:
I loved this. Made it using garlic salt instead of garlic powder. And doubled the chicken broth/stock. (used 2 cups instead of 1).

I used thinner cut chops, since that is what I had on hand. I used 7 thin chops. It did not take 4 hours on high, only about 3 hrs.

At the end, I added some corn starch and cold water (2 TBLS corn starch with a small amount of water) to thicken up the gravy. I let that sit in the crock on high while I finished the rice & sides.

Served over Basamati Rice with roasted broccoli as a side.

It was an easy delicious meal. A good change of pace to my usual pork chop recipe. I will make again.

Although my husband did comment that he thought the meat was dry...and then I told him it was pork chops and he said, "oh ok. That's why". (He had thought it was a chicken dish)

text:
I tried this recipe out of sheer laziness.  I only started making pork chops a year or so ago and while the recipe I have been using is fantastic, it is labor intensive/time consuming.  That just wasn't in the cards today.  I had all of the ingredients on-hand for this one (which suggests that we would like them) so I thought I'd give it a whirl.  It took all of 3 minutes to whisk the seasonings together and throw everything in the crock.   I must have heard at least 10 times how delicious they smelled while they were cooking and the end result was no different...SCRUMPTIOUS!!!  They were super moist and fell apart while fishing them out of the crock.  

I pretty much stuck to the original recipe  - I was out of oregano so I substituted Italian seasoning and cut the basil in half, used Old Bay Seasoning as the poultry seasoning and 2 tsp minced garlic rather than mincing fresh cloves.  My husband absolutely LOVED these and they were oh-so-easy.  

I served the chops with a long grain wild rice medley boiled in a mix of 1/2 water & 1/2 of the drippings from the crock pot, as I was unsure of how strong the seasoning would be. The rice had a nice flavor and was not overly seasoned.  I might even try making it with 1/4 water & 3/4 drippings next time.  Recommended cooking time was spot on for my Rival Smart-Pot crock pot (I think it's a 5-qt).  

Thank you for sharing this recipe - it's nice to find another yummy pork chop recipe that doesn't turn out like a rubber dog toy!  :)

For the greens, I cooked them in some of the extra sauce from the pork chops.  I will definitely make again!

text:
My 4 year old had 4 helpings!! My husband thanked me 3-4 time more than he normally does. He didn't add anything to his plate (usually he adds some kind of spice). I started with frozen pork chops, cooked it on high for 4 hours in the sauce. I was worried that not doing it on low for 8-10 hours would make for tougher meat. But it was soooooooo tender, fell right off our forks. I used garlic salt instead of garlic powder and ommitted the additional salt & pepper. I also used Mesquite chicken seasoning, cause it was all I had on hand. And I used 2 cups of homemade chicken stock. I served it with rice & green beans. The sauce went great with both sides - I wish it had been a bit thicker, but the rice soaked it right up. I WILL make this again. VERY easy and was a hit with everyone!

text:
This recipe is very WEIRD!  The flavors just don't go well together.  I followed the recipe almost exactly- the only thing I did different was add a few extra garlic cloves and an onion.  Both of which I couldn't even taste.  Other reviewers are correct when they say the herbs are way too overpowering.  For me it was the poultry seasoning.  That's all I can taste!!  The cooking times are also off.  Mine were falling apart after 2.5 hours on high.  My husband complained about them being dry- maybe it's because the recipe calls for poking holes in the pork?  I've always been told not to do that with meats because it lets the juices out.  The sauce is a nice consistency, but again, it just tastes like poultry seasoning.  This is an over-rated recipe IMHO, and for those who plan to try it- have a back up plan for dinner.

My family loved the meal, however I made a few changes.  I browned country style pork ribs in a tablespoon of olive oil.  Transferred the meat into a crock pot.  Pan fried one onion and a couple cloves of garlic in whatever oil was left in the pan.  Transferred it into crock pot.  I took the advice of another reviewer and made gravy from the sauce.  I only took 2 cups of sauce to make the gravy b/c there's lots.  Be sure to sift the sauce so you don't have lumps in your gravy. YUMMY!!!

These were definately melt in your mouth tender!  I used bone-in pork chops and they were literally falling off the bone...   I sauteed oinions and garlic and layed them at the bottom of the slow cooker before putting the pork chops in.  I doubled the chicken broth and used all the seasoning suggested... added a dash of balsamic vin.   I cooked it on low for 7 hours.   I tried adding potatoes in at about the half way point but I found that the strong herbs are a little to overwhelming for the potatoes so wouldn't recommend that.  I'd go with other vieweres suggestion for rice or mashed potatoes as a side vs. trying to add potatoes or veggies to the pot.  The meat will be the star of the meal with this recipe - definately a tasty recipe to try!!

text:
Wonderful flavors are bursting in my mouth as I reveiw this recipe!

Outside of recalculating  for the 3 thick boneless chops I had, I followed the recipe to a tee + added approximately a 1/2 cup of some leftover sauerkraut.

I cooked mine on high for one hour, low the next, high again the next & back to low for the final hour.  Switched the setting over to keep warm while I made some buttred garlic egg-free noodles and french style green beans.

The chops came out absolutley juicy and tender as promised but,  a little too salty for my liking so next time, I'll omit the salt to season the chops.

Oh yeah,  I added all the ingredients to the crockpot to avoid making an unneccessary dish and, I browned the chops very lightly before adding them to the pot.

Everyone really needs to give this recipe a try!!!

Thanks Bunches 4 Posting It!

text:
I followed the advice of others and doubled the chicken broth (and then added another half cup more because I threw in 6 pork chops but kept the recipe the same). I also cut up fresh mushrooms and onion and layered those in with the pork chops. I served this to my dad and boyfriend and they both thought it was great. I used the mushrooms and onions as garnish instead of the broth and so they weren't too oily and the flavor was nice and light. I would definitely make this recipe again.

I cook for only 2 of us, so I am always looking for recipes that can easily be cut down and wonâ€™t leave me with a half a can of soup or something like that. For this recipe, I used 2 extra-thick cut bones chops and cut the ingredients in the sauce recipe by half. I served the chops with rice. I thought there was plenty of sauce, so am not sure why so many people talked about doubling the amount of sauce-wow! Anyway, the chops were very tender and flavorful, although I think I will cut down on the amount of paprika next time. I cooked this according to the original recipe. I think I will try it next time with the addition of some small red potatoes or cut up a larger russet potato and maybe some pearl onions and cook on low heat for 7-8 hours. I agree with another reviewer who noted that this would probably be a great recipe using a pork roast too.

https://images.media-allrecipes.com/userphotos/50x50/6652468.jpg
city:
None
region:
None
country:
None
text:
This was very good.  I used 4 bone-in pork chops (not thick).  I scattered 1/2 large onion in the bottom of the crockpot, cut back the paprika to 1t, and oregano to 1/2t.  Added 2 huge cloves of garlic and omitted the garlic powder.  Used 2 cups of beef broth because that's all I had on hand.  I cooked it on low for 6 hours, then removed and covered the chops, and added 1 cup of jasmati rice.  Cooked another 45 mins or so, then added back the pork chops, and cooked for about 30 more minutes.  Tender, falling off the bone pork and such flavorful rice.  I think that those whose chops were dry and/or tough either didn't add enough broth, didn't cook it long enough on low, or cooked it on high.  Low and slow is the way to go!

text:
One of the delicious recipes for slow cooked pork chops! Definitely a keeper and will add this to my recipe library. 
It had a Mediterranean taste to it but I thought it wouldn't hurt if I add 1 tsp balsamic vinegar and 1 tsp Worcestershire sauce. I got worried it might be too garlic-y so I added 1/4 cup of chopped onions. I had 9 pork chops to cook so I double the sauce measurements. One of the reviewers said that she browned the chops first which I did. I put a little bit salt and pepper on the 1-inch pork chops and browned them first for more flavor (about 3-4 minutes on each side) before putting them into the crockpot. I cooked them in low for 8 hours. I added some roasted peppers that I already have in my fridge before serving. Do a final taste with the sauce. Mine came in a little bit short with salt so I had to put a little more in. Every bite of the pork chop was delish. It is extremely moist that it doesn't taste like pork chops! LOL

I made this pretty much exactly by the recipe. I had a package of 7 thick cut boneless chops, so I used 1 and 1 half amounts on all the seasonings and oil, and used a whole (almost 2 cups) can of chicken broth. It was perfect, very delicious! I let them cook longer than called for on low and they were super tender and the extra broth kept them nice and moist. My fiance and his daughter both liked them a lot. She actually is very lucky and likes mostly plain good, but did great with these. I agree with someone else who said they have a but of a Mediterranean flavor, but it's not strong or overwhelming. I'm definitely making these again.

Hey! So some background first - I'm a 15 year old EXTREMELY inexperienced chef, but this was soOOO easy to make. And it was delicious! Whole family loved it(parents, brother, and brother's girlfriend) and I will definitely be making it again!

text:
I made this today. I had to look up a slow cooker recipe because my fan oven broke & I came across this which looked easy enough for a novice.
I used 'bone-in' pork chops. I used a chicken stock cube instead of broth. I didn't have 'poultry seasoning' so googled what it was & added small amounts of each ingredient to the mixture (sage, rosemary, thyme, marjoram & black pepper).
I actually think the chops were cooked after 3 hours so I turned it onto a 'low' setting for the last hour. I didn't baste because the liquid covered the chops so I turned them over half way through.
I didn't have any corn flour so I made up some chicken gravy granules with water & whisked them in with the sauce to make a gravy.
The meat fell off the bone & was so tender & tasty. I served it with baby potatoes, chantennay carrots & corn. It was a MASSIVE hit with my husband and two VERY fussy young sons. The gravy was lush...!
I will definitely be making this again. Many thanks from the O'Brien family for this wonderful recipe.

text:
I made this and followed many of the reviewers ideas. I added an extra cup of broth and cooked on low for 8 hours.  There was no need to baste then because the broth covered the chops the entire time. But I agree with those that said you do NOT take the lid off the crock pot. I added more garlic, because I love garlic. I did make gravy out of the juice that was left and it was good on the meat and mashed potatoes.  I don't love pork chops, even though these literally fell apart coming out of the crock pot, pork chops are still a dry meat.  But the gravy helped.  I will make this again when I need something other than chicken or beef.  It's nice to put something in the crock pot and not worry about it.

text:
** this broth makes an amazing gravy. 

Followed almost exactly, except:
1- I doubled the recipe. 
2- I had no basil, so I substituted that ingredient with herbes de Provence. 
3- I purposefully went a little heavy on the oregano. 
4- I ended up using "better than bouillon" to make my broth because that's what I had. Worked great. 
I LOVED how this turned out. I will definitely be making it again. Soooo easy. 

**For the gravy after, I ladled it nearly all of the juices into a saucepan, brought it to a boil. Meanwhile, I whisked about 1/3 c of flour into  ~ 1 1/2 -2 c of milk, and then slowly whisked the mixture into my boiling juices. Let it boil for about a minute once fully combined. Done. It was seriously so good.

text:
This was really tasty.  We doubled the gravy ingredients (except for the olive oil 1/3 cup instead of a 1/2 cup - and it was still too much oil).  We had some 2 inch thick bone-in pork chops and we felt would be good for this recipe.  Unfortunately the chops turned out dry, no fault to the recipe.  I probably over cooked them.  I removed the chops to a plate and poured the gravy into a sauce pan. I added about 1/3 cup 1% milk, brought it to a slow boil and added some 1 tablespoon of cornstarch dissolved it in a little cold water to thicken gravy. The gravy was delicious over some white jasmine rice.  I did cut the poultry seasoning back to half because it is strong and I didn't want it to over power the gravy.  It was the right decision.  I also cut the garlic powder back to 2 tsp. instead of 2 tablespoons since fresh garlic is part of the recipe.  I didn't want it to be too garlicy. Again I feel was the right decision.  I will definitely be making this again, next time with smaller cut pork chops which should work better.  Next time I will cut the olive back to 1 -2 tablespoons for a double gravy or just not ad it at all.  I don't know why so much oil was included in this recipe because it's definitely not needed because the chops produce fat to the gravy as well. A few reviewers stated it tasted Mediterranean but my hubby and I disagree.  It is a strong flavor set though.

text:
We've made this twice now - just for us a few weeks ago and last night with my in-laws as guests- and it was a hit both times. Even our 6 year old daughter happily took leftovers in her lunch today. We have the All Clad Slow Cooker, whose cast -aluminum insert can be used on the stove top. I lightly browned the chops right in that before adding the rest of the ingredients, though this step really wouldn't be necessary and I'd likely skip it if crunched for time. No need to cut slits in the chops. The only thing I would definitely change is the cooking time.  The first time I made the recipe, my chops were under 1 inch thick and average size. I cooked them 2 hours on low and they were good, if not a little dry. This time I used pork chops from Costco and they're huge, about 7-8 oz each( I weighed them), and over 1 inch thick. I can't eat a whole one myself.  They ended up being cooked almost 5 hours on low (I intended 4 hours, but our guests came late) and, again, they were just a little dry for my preference. I really think 3.5-4 hours would be perfect. I also added 2 containers of sliced baby portabellas each time during the last 20 mins of cooking and they turned out to be an excellent addition to the broth over rice. The next time I think I'll add a sliced onion at the beginning, too.  This recipe is great as written (except for cooking time, but that may be due to my particular slow cooker) and has been added to our regular rotation. I might even bake it in the oven the n

text:
I didn't change a lot. First of all, experienced cooks know that a tablespoon of dried herbs/spices can be overpowering because the flavors get concentrated when herbs are dried. So I used about half the quantity the recipe called for. I added a sliced onion along with the browned chops and the rest of the ingredients. Cooked on low for several hours. I added a touch of tarragon vinegar to the sauce at the end and then thickened with a roux. Results were very, very good. Even my husband, who avoids eating meat, enjoyed this dish. I served it with roasted small red potatoes and a green salad. Definitely will make again.

To be fair, we didn't exactly follow the receipe but rather used it as a guide. We seasoned 2 pork chops with salt, pepper, garlic and red pepper flakes. Seared on both sides for 1-2 mins/side. We put in the crockpot for 4 hours on low w/ 2 cups chicken broth, 1 cup white wine, 1 tbsp of Dales low sodium seasoning and 1/2 a medium white onion. After the 4 hours were up we made a gravy with the remaining juice and poured it over rice.

Had I ordered them in a restaurant I wouldn't have sent them back for something else, but they weren't so good that I would have stuffed myself beyond being full or even bothered taking home any leftovers. I don't agree with the review that says don't baste because you want to retain the heat in the crock pot - it's not a pressure cooker so letting out heat won't hurt it, it'll heat up again & pork chops do benefit from basting when they don't have sauce that covers the top.

Extremely tasty!! I wanted big bold flavors in my pork chops because I was sick of the same ol' breaded and fried chops. I thickened the sauce with cornstrach to get a nice gravy and served it over egg noodles. I will make this recipe again, again, and again! Though I will add that when you make this recipe, make sure you have a very thick cut of pork chops. I made it the first time with regular sized pork chop sirloins (shame on me!) and all though the flavor was there, the actual meat was a little tough.
